font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>'''Çandarlı Kara Halil Hayreddin Pasha''' ({{lang-ota|<del style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">چاندارلی</del> کارا حلیل خير الدين پاشا}}) was the first [[Grand Viziers of the Ottoman Empire|Grand Vizier]] of [[Murad I]]'s reign. He was also technically the first in [[Ottoman Empire|Ottoman]] history who held the title "[[Grand Vizier of the Ottoman Empire|Grand Vizier]]" (although several before him held equivalent but differently named offices), the first who had a military background (his predecessors under [[Orhan]] came from the class of learned men, the "''ilmiye''"), and the first member of the illustrious [[Çandarlı family]] to hold high office. His family was to mark the rise of the [[Ottoman Empire]] between 1360 and 1450.&lt;ref name = googbook&gt;Encyclopedia of the Ottoman Empire. Gábor Ágoston, Bruce Alan Masters. p.398&lt;/ref&gt; He was a successful commander, setting the precedent for centuries of Ottoman presence in Albania after his victory at the [[Battle of Savra]].</div></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>'''Çandarlı Kara Halil Hayreddin Pasha''' ({{lang-ota|<ins style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">چندارلی</ins> کارا حلیل خير الدين پاشا}}) was the first [[Grand Viziers of the Ottoman Empire|Grand Vizier]] of [[Murad I]]'s reign. He was also technically the first in [[Ottoman Empire|Ottoman]] history who held the title "[[Grand Vizier of the Ottoman Empire|Grand Vizier]]" (although several before him held equivalent but differently named offices), the first who had a military background (his predecessors under [[Orhan]] came from the class of learned men, the "''ilmiye''"), and the first member of the illustrious [[Çandarlı family]] to hold high office. His family was to mark the rise of the [[Ottoman Empire]] between 1360 and 1450.&lt;ref name = googbook&gt;Encyclopedia of the Ottoman Empire. Gábor Ágoston, Bruce Alan Masters. p.398&lt;/ref&gt; He was a successful commander, setting the precedent for centuries of Ottoman presence in Albania after his victory at the [[Battle of Savra]].</div></td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></td> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>He rose to the rank of grand vizier from the position of the chief military judge (''[[kazasker]]'') in September 1364 and held this top seat after the sultan until his death on January 22, 1387. He died in Serrai during the Ottoman campaign on Macedonia.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book |last1=Imber |first1=Colin |title=The Ottoman Empire, 1300-1481 |date=1990 |publisher=The Isis Press Istanbul}}&lt;/ref&gt; As such, he became the grand vizier who had the longest term of administration, a record he would hold until the abolition of the position 535 years after his death in 1922. He was also notable for being the initiator of the "[[devşirme]]" system of recruitment in the Ottoman Empire. Çandarlı Kara Halil Pasha is not to be confused with his grandson, [[Çandarlı Halil Pasha the Younger]], grand vizier under the reign of [[Murad II]] and during the first years of that of [[Mehmed II]].</div></td> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>He rose to the rank of grand vizier from the position of the chief military judge (''[[kazasker]]'') in September 1364 and held this top seat after the sultan until his death on January 22, 1387. He died in Serrai during the Ottoman campaign on Macedonia.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book |last1=Imber |first1=Colin |title=The Ottoman Empire, 1300-1481 |date=1990 |publisher=The Isis Press Istanbul}}&lt;/ref&gt; As such, he became the grand vizier who had the longest term of administration, a record he would hold until the abolition of the position 535 years after his death in 1922. He was also notable for being the initiator of the "[[devşirme]]" system of recruitment in the Ottoman Empire. Çandarlı Kara Halil Pasha is not to be confused with his grandson, [[Çandarlı Halil Pasha the Younger]], grand vizier under the reign of [[Murad II]] and during the first years of that of [[Mehmed II]].</div></td> </tr> <!-- diff cache key enwiki:diff:1.41:old-1220123938:rev-1220124001:wikidiff2=table:1.14.1:ff290eae --> </table> 92.9.142.156 https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bob_Dylan&diff=1220124002&oldid=1219851053 Bob Dylan 2024-04-21T23:49:23Z <p>Rescuing 1 sources and tagging 0 as dead.) #IABot (v2.0.9.5</p> <table style="background-color: #fff; color: #202122;" data-mw="interface"> <col class="diff-marker" /> <col class="diff-content" /> <col class="diff-marker" /> <col class="diff-content" /> <tr class="diff-title" lang="en"> <td colspan="2" style="background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;">← Previous revision</td> <td colspan="2" style="background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;">Revision as of 23:49, 21 April 2024</td> </tr><tr> <td colspan="2" class="diff-lineno">Line 248:</td> <td colspan="2" class="diff-lineno">Line 248:</td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div> |description= Dylan's [[Academy Award|Oscar]]-winning song was featured in the movie ''[[Wonder Boys (film)|Wonder Boys]]''. Recorded with his touring band, Dylan produced the album under the alias Jack Frost.&lt;ref&gt;Gray (2006), pp. 556–557.&lt;/ref&gt; Critics noted that Dylan was widening his musical palette to include [[rockabilly]], [[Western swing]], [[jazz]] and [[lounge music]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite magazine |url=https://ew.com/ew/article/0,,173933~4~~lovetheft,00.html |title=''Love and Theft''|access-date=September 7, 2008 |magazine=Entertainment Weekly |date=October 1, 2001}}&lt;/ref&gt; The album won the [[Grammy Award for Best Contemporary Folk Album]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web| url =https://www.awardsandshows.com/features/best-contemporary-folk-album-255.html| title =Best Contemporary Folk Album | access-date = February 20, 2024| website = awardsandshows.com}}&lt;/ref&gt; Controversy ensued when ''[[The Wall Street Journal]]'' pointed out similarities between the album's lyrics and [[Junichi Saga]]'s book ''[[Confessions of a Yakuza]]''. Saga was not familiar with Dylan's work, but said he was flattered. Upon hearing the album, Saga said of Dylan: "His lines flow from one image to the next and don't always make sense. But they have a great atmosphere."&lt;ref&gt;This is a reprint of the article from ''The Wall Street Journal'' cited in next footnote.{{cite news|url=http://www.csudh.edu/dearhabermas/plagiarbk010.htm |title=Did Bob Dylan Lift Lines From Dr Saga? |access-date=September 29, 2011 |publisher=California State University, Dear Habermas |date=July 8, 2003 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080724053350/http://www.csudh.edu/dearhabermas/plagiarbk010.htm |archive-date=July 24, 2008 }}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news| url = https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10576176194220600| title = Did Bob Dylan Lift Lines From Dr Saga?| access-date=September 29, 2011| work = [[The Wall Street Journal]]| date = July 8, 2003}}&lt;/ref&gt; </div></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>In 2001, Dylan won an [[Academy Award for Best Original Song]] for "[[Things Have Changed]]", written for the film ''[[Wonder Boys (film)|Wonder Boys]]''.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://awardsdatabase.oscars.org/ampas_awards/DisplayMain.jsp?curTime=1365675507836 |title=The Academy of Motion Pictures Arts and Science&amp;nbsp;– 2000 Awards |access-date=April 12, 2013 |publisher=awardsdatabase.oscars.org/ |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140407061952/http://awardsdatabase.oscars.org/ampas_awards/DisplayMain.jsp?curTime=1365675507836 |archive-date=April 7, 2014 }}&lt;/ref&gt; ''[["Love and Theft"]]'' was released on September 11, 2001. font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>Filming took place primarily in [[New Orleans]] and in [[London]], with limited location shooting done in [[San Francisco]] and [[Paris]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite AV media| title=Interview with the Vampire End Credits| publisher=Geffen Pictures| date=1994}}&lt;/ref&gt; Louis' plantation was a combination of primarily [[Destrehan Plantation]], just west&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web|url=https://www.google.com/maps/place/Destrehan+Plantation/@29.8878509,-90.2450303,10.91z/data=!4m5!3m4!1s0x8620c5e7be95ae1b:0x6cf7f142d99adc8e!8m2!3d29.945408!4d-90.3652365?shorturl=1|title=Destrehan Plantation|website=Google Maps|language=en|access-date=2019-06-03}}&lt;/ref&gt; of New Orleans, and [[Oak Alley Plantation]] in nearby [[Vacherie]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite magazine| url=http://deepsouthmag.com/2013/10/04/movies-filmed-on-louisiana-plantations/| title=Movies Filmed on Louisiana Plantations|first=Erin Z. |last=Bass|magazine=Deep South Magazine| date=2013-10-04|access-date=2017-11-30}}&lt;/ref&gt; The depiction of 18th- and early-19th-century New Orleans was achieved with a combination of location shooting in the [[French Quarter]] of New Orleans and filming on a purpose-built waterfront set along the [[Mississippi <del style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">river</del>]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite video| title=Commentary by Director Neil Jordan| publisher=Warner Home Video| medium= DVD| year=2008}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name="movie-locations.com"&gt;{{cite web| url=http://www.movie-locations.com/movies/i/interview.html| archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20020505084343/http://www.movie-locations.com/movies/i/interview.html| url-status=dead| archive-date=May 5, 2002| title=Film locations for Interview with the Vampire| website=movie-locations.com| access-date=2017-11-30}}&lt;/ref&gt; Production then moved to [[London]], where interior sets were constructed at [[Pinewood Studios]].&lt;ref name="Mike Scott"&gt;{{cite news| title=Brad Pitt says 'Interview with the Vampire' was a 'Miserable' Experience| first=Mike |last=Scott |newspaper=The Times Picayune| date=2011-09-24}}&lt;/ref&gt; The sets designed by Dante Ferretti included the interiors of Louis, Lestat and Claudia's New Orleans townhouse, Claudia and Louis' Paris hotel suite, the Théâtre des Vampires (built on Pinewood's [[007 Stage]]), and the catacombs where the Parisian vampires live.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite AV media| title=Commentary by Director Neil Jordan| publisher=Warner Home Video| date=2008}}&lt;/ref&gt; Shooting took place in San Francisco, mainly on the [[Golden Gate Bridge]], with the external façade of Louis' hotel located at the intersection of Taylor Street, [[Market Street (San Francisco)|Market Street]], and Golden Gate Avenue.&lt;ref name="movie-locations.com"/&gt; In Paris the exterior and lobby of the [[Opera Garnier]] were dressed to film Louis and Claudia's arrival at their hotel in Paris.</div></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>[[Sacramento International Airport]] {{Airport codes|SMF|KSMF|SMF}} is a public [[airport]] {{convert|10|mi|abbr=off|sp=us}} northwest of downtown Sacramento, in [[Sacramento County, California]]. [[Southwest Airlines]] is the dominant passenger airline with more than 104 daily flights to 25 cities across the US.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web |title=City Fact Sheets |url=http://swamedia.com/ |access-date=2023-04-29 |website=Southwest Airlines Newsroom |language=en}}&lt;/ref&gt; Other airlines include [[Delta Air Lines|Delta]], [[United Airlines|United]], [[Spirit Airlines]], [[American Airlines]] and [[Alaska Airlines]]. The airport handles flights to and from various US destinations (including Hawaii) as well as Mexico, Canada and connecting flights to Europe, Asia, and South America, and served more than 13&amp;nbsp;million passengers in 2019.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=https://sacramento.aero/download.php?f=/January_2022_Web_Report.pdf|website=Sacramento County|title=Passenger Statistics |access-date=February 22, 2022}}&lt;/ref&gt; The airport is well known for the {{convert|56|ft|m|-long|adj=mid}} red aluminum rabbit titled "Leap" by [[Lawrence Argent]] in Terminal B.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.sacbee.com/news/business/article3498199.html|title=Sacramento airport's big red rabbit means business – really|work=The Sacramento Bee|access-date=November 15, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151117015624/http://www.sacbee.com/news/business/article3498199.html|archive-date=November 17, 2015|url-status=live}}&lt;/ref&gt;</div></td> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>[[Sacramento International Airport]] {{Airport codes|SMF|KSMF|SMF}} is a public [[airport]] {{convert|10|mi|abbr=off|sp=us}} northwest of downtown Sacramento, in [[Sacramento County, California]]. [[Southwest Airlines]] is the dominant passenger airline with more than 104 daily flights to 25 cities across the US.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite web |title=City Fact Sheets |url=http://swamedia.com/ |access-date=2023-04-29 |website=Southwest Airlines Newsroom |language=en}}&lt;/ref&gt; Other airlines include [[Delta Air Lines|Delta]], [[United Airlines|United]], [[Spirit Airlines]], [[American Airlines]] and [[Alaska Airlines]]. The airport handles flights to and from various US destinations (including Hawaii) as well as Mexico, Canada and connecting flights to Europe, Asia, and South America, and served more than 13&amp;nbsp;million passengers in 2019.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=https://sacramento.aero/download.php?f=/January_2022_Web_Report.pdf|website=Sacramento County|title=Passenger Statistics |access-date=February 22, 2022}}&lt;/ref&gt; The airport is well known for the {{convert|56|ft|m|-long|adj=mid}} red aluminum rabbit titled "Leap" by [[Lawrence Argent]] in Terminal B.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.sacbee.com/news/business/article3498199.html|title=Sacramento airport's big red rabbit means business – really|work=The Sacramento Bee|access-date=November 15, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151117015624/http://www.sacbee.com/news/business/article3498199.html|archive-date=November 17, 2015|url-status=live}}&lt;/ref&gt;</div></td> </tr> <tr> <td colspan="2" class="diff-empty diff-side-deleted"></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></td> </tr> <tr> <td colspan="2" class="diff-empty diff-side-deleted"></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>[[Sacramento McClellan Airport]] {{airport codes|MCC|KMCC|MCC}} is a privately-owned, public-use [[airport]] located in the unincorporated area of [[McClellan Park, California]], {{Convert|6|mi|km nmi|abbr=out|spell=in}} northeast of the [[central business district]] of [[Sacramento, California|Sacramento]]. The airport is on the former site of '''[[McClellan Air Force Base]]''', which existed as a military base from 1939 to 2000. It was transferred to Sacramento County in 2000, as part of its conversion into McClellan Business Park, and was purchased by McClellan Business Park in October 2017. The airport is a public-use facility which operates as an uncontrolled airfield in what the FAA designates as Class "E" Airspace. The airport is mainly used for general aviation.</div></td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>In [[Greek mythology]], '''Kratos''', also known as '''Cratus<del style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;">,</del>''' '''Cratos''',{{efn|[[Ancient Greek language|Ancient Greek]]: {{lang|grc|Κράτος}}, usually [[Transliteration|transliterated]] as ''Krátos'', but sometimes [[Romanization of Greek|Latinized]] as ''Cratus'' or ''Cratos''. The name literally means "Power"{{sfn|Ruffell|2012|page=25}}{{sfn|Martin|2016|page=163}} or "Strength".{{sfn|Lowe|2009|page=82}}&lt;ref&gt;{{LSJ|kra/tos1|κράτος|ref}}.&lt;/ref&gt;}}<del style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;"> or '''John Kratos'''</del> is the divine personification of strength. He is the son of [[Pallas (Titan)|Pallas]] and [[Styx#Goddess|Styx]]. Kratos and his siblings [[Nike (mythology)|Nike]] ('Victory'), [[Bia (mythology)|Bia]] ('Force'), and [[Zelus]] ('Glory') are all the personification of a specific trait.&lt;ref&gt;Gantz, pp. 25&amp;ndash;26 (the translations given here are Gantz's); [[Hesiod]], ''[[Theogony]]'' [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0020.tlg001.perseus-eng1:371-403 383&amp;ndash;385]; [[Bibliotheca (Pseudo-Apollodorus)|Apollodorus]] [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0548.tlg001.perseus-eng1:1.2.4 1.2.4]&lt;/ref&gt; Kratos is first mentioned alongside his siblings in [[Hesiod]]'s ''[[Theogony]]''. According to Hesiod, Kratos and his siblings dwell with [[Zeus]] because their mother Styx came to him first to request a position in his regime, so he honored her and her children with exalted positions. Kratos and his sister Bia are best known for their appearance in the opening scene of [[Aeschylus]]' ''[[Prometheus Bound]]''. Acting as agents of Zeus, they lead the captive [[Titan (mythology)|Titan]] [[Prometheus]] on stage. Kratos compels the mild-mannered blacksmith god [[Hephaestus]] to chain Prometheus to a rock as punishment for his theft of fire.&lt;ref&gt;Gantz, p. 158; [[Aeschylus]] (?), ''[[Prometheus Bound]]'', [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0085.tlg003.perseus-eng1:1-35 1 ff.]&lt;/ref&gt;</div></td> <td class="diff-marker" data-marker="+"></td> <td style="color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>In [[Greek mythology]], '''Kratos''', also known as '''Cratus'''<ins style="font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;"> or</ins> '''Cratos''',{{efn|[[Ancient Greek language|Ancient Greek]]: {{lang|grc|Κράτος}}, usually [[Transliteration|transliterated]] as ''Krátos'', but sometimes [[Romanization of Greek|Latinized]] as ''Cratus'' or ''Cratos''. The name literally means "Power"{{sfn|Ruffell|2012|page=25}}{{sfn|Martin|2016|page=163}} or "Strength".{{sfn|Lowe|2009|page=82}}&lt;ref&gt;{{LSJ|kra/tos1|κράτος|ref}}.&lt;/ref&gt;}} is the divine personification of strength. He is the son of [[Pallas (Titan)|Pallas]] and [[Styx#Goddess|Styx]]. Kratos and his siblings [[Nike (mythology)|Nike]] ('Victory'), [[Bia (mythology)|Bia]] ('Force'), and [[Zelus]] ('Glory') are all the personification of a specific trait.&lt;ref&gt;Gantz, pp. 25&amp;ndash;26 (the translations given here are Gantz's); [[Hesiod]], ''[[Theogony]]'' [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0020.tlg001.perseus-eng1:371-403 383&amp;ndash;385]; [[Bibliotheca (Pseudo-Apollodorus)|Apollodorus]] [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0548.tlg001.perseus-eng1:1.2.4 1.2.4]&lt;/ref&gt; Kratos is first mentioned alongside his siblings in [[Hesiod]]'s ''[[Theogony]]''. According to Hesiod, Kratos and his siblings dwell with [[Zeus]] because their mother Styx came to him first to request a position in his regime, so he honored her and her children with exalted positions. Kratos and his sister Bia are best known for their appearance in the opening scene of [[Aeschylus]]' ''[[Prometheus Bound]]''. Acting as agents of Zeus, they lead the captive [[Titan (mythology)|Titan]] [[Prometheus]] on stage. Kratos compels the mild-mannered blacksmith god [[Hephaestus]] to chain Prometheus to a rock as punishment for his theft of fire.&lt;ref&gt;Gantz, p. 158; [[Aeschylus]] (?), ''[[Prometheus Bound]]'', [http://data.perseus.org/citations/urn:cts:greekLit:tlg0085.tlg003.perseus-eng1:1-35 1 ff.]&lt;/ref&gt;</div></td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></td> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><br /></td> </tr> <tr> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>Kratos is characterized as brutal and merciless, repeatedly mocking both Hephaestus and Prometheus and advocating for the use of unnecessary violence. He defends Zeus' oppressive rule and predicts that Prometheus will never escape his bonds. In Aeschylus' ''[[Libation Bearers]]'', [[Electra]] calls upon Kratos, [[Dike (mythology)|Dike]] ("Justice"), and Zeus to aid her brother [[Orestes]] in avenging the murder of their father [[Agamemnon]]. Kratos and Bia appear in a late fifth-century BC [[red-figure]] Attic ''[[skyphos]]'' of the punishment of [[Ixion]], possibly based on a scene from a lost tragedy by [[Euripides]]. They also appear in late eighteenth and nineteenth-century [[Romanticism|Romantic]] depictions and adaptations of the binding of Prometheus. </div></td> <td class="diff-marker"></td> <td style="background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;"><div>Kratos is characterized as brutal and merciless, repeatedly mocking both Hephaestus and Prometheus and advocating for the use of unnecessary violence.
